## OntologyMaker_process

| Purpose                                                                                                                                                                                                             |
|:--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| This glossary was developed to clarify and align terminology used in the emerging metaverse ecosystem.                                                                                                              |
| It provides a common language for organisations working across technology, governance, creative and industrial sectors, helping ensure interoperability between frameworks and standards.                           |
| 1. Source Selection                                                                                                                                                                                                 |
| Authoritative materials were reviewed across four principal categories:                                                                                                                                             |
| Standards and reference architectures — e.g. ETSI, ISO/IEC, IEEE.                                                                                                                                                   |
| Metaverse and web taxonomies — e.g. Metaverse Standards Forum (MSF) and affiliated registries.                                                                                                                      |
| Data and identity frameworks — e.g. W3C PROV-O, DCAT, DID, XR Accessibility.                                                                                                                                        |
| Sectoral and cultural frameworks — e.g. UNESCO, OECD, SMPTE, SIGGRAPH.                                                                                                                                              |
| Sources were prioritised for breadth of use, open availability, and international recognition.                                                                                                                      |
| 2. Term Identification and Harmonisation                                                                                                                                                                            |
| Terminology was extracted directly from published standards, use-case libraries, and taxonomy documents.                                                                                                            |
| Equivalent or overlapping terms were reconciled to a single preferred label following ISO/IEC drafting conventions.                                                                                                 |
| Each entry received a unique identifier for traceability.                                                                                                                                                           |
| 3. Source Attribution                                                                                                                                                                                               |
| Every term was linked to the specific frameworks, working groups, or organisations in which it appears or is formally defined.                                                                                      |
| Where multiple authorities reference a concept, these are listed together to show the scope of agreement.                                                                                                           |
| 4. Consensus Level (TermMaturity)                                                                                                                                                                                   |
| Each term was assigned a mode value indicating how widely it is referenced across independent sources:                                                                                                              |
| 4–5 — Widely standardised across multiple frameworks                                                                                                                                                                |
| 3 — Recognised by several authorities                                                                                                                                                                               |
| 2 — Emerging consensus                                                                                                                                                                                              |
| 1 — Specialised or under development                                                                                                                                                                                |
| This provides a clear indicator of maturity without reproducing definitions.                                                                                                                                        |
| 5. Conceptual Framework                                                                                                                                                                                             |
| To organise terminology consistently across technical, experiential, and governance layers, the glossary adopts a three-domain model derived from converging standards initiatives.                                 |
| Each term is positioned within one or more intersecting domains drawn from ETSI and the Metaverse Standards Forum (MSF).                                                                                            |
| This tri-domain approach enables users to interpret where a concept operates within the wider metaverse ecosystem.                                                                                                  |
| 1. Functional Architecture (ETSI Domain)                                                                                                                                                                            |
| The ETSI Metaverse Reference Architecture Framework (ARF) defines core functional domains describing how metaverse systems are structured and interconnected.                                                       |
| These domains focus on infrastructure, computation, interaction, trust, and content management.                                                                                                                     |
| They form the baseline for understanding system-level interoperability and technical performance.                                                                                                                   |
| 2. Structural Taxonomy (MSF Education WG)                                                                                                                                                                           |
| The EWG taxonomy introduces structural layers describing how metaverse environments are assembled—from the physical and network infrastructure up to application and experience layers.                             |
| This classification captures how different technologies (e.g. rendering, data synchronisation, AI processing) interact within a stack.                                                                              |
| It bridges between low-level system functions and user-facing experiences.                                                                                                                                          |
| 3. Application and Use Case Context (MSF Use Cases / Taxonomy)                                                                                                                                                      |
| The Metaverse Standards Forum (MSF) defines aspects and verticals that describe how technologies are applied in practice—covering creative industries, education, industrial use, digital identity, and governance. |
| These “verticals” provide a lens on domain-specific adoption rather than technical implementation.                                                                                                                  |
| 6. Review and Validation                                                                                                                                                                                            |
| Entries were reviewed in thematic clusters—identity, infrastructure, creative media, ethics, and governance—to ensure consistency.                                                                                  |
| Cross-sector terms were validated against overlapping domains to confirm appropriate usage and avoid duplication.                                                                                                   |
| 6. Deliverables                                                                                                                                                                                                     |
| The glossary is provided as a structured dataset containing:                                                                                                                                                        |
| Unique identifier (ID)                                                                                                                                                                                              |
| Preferred term                                                                                                                                                                                                      |
| Definition (standards style)                                                                                                                                                                                        |
| 3 x domain categorisation (functional, structural, application)                                                                                                                                                     |
| Mode value (consensus indicator)                                                                                                                                                                                    |
| Associated standards or reference sources                                                                                                                                                                           |
| The dataset is formatted for integration with ontology and interoperability tools and for reference in standards development activities.                                                                            |
| 7. Use and Licensing                                                                                                                                                                                                |
| The glossary is designed for educational, research, and cross-sector collaboration purposes.                                                                                                                        |
| It may be cited or incorporated into standards work provided appropriate attribution is given to the contributing organisations and source standards.                                                               |


=== metaverse_glossary_logseq_examples.md ===
# Metaverse Glossary - Logseq Ontology Example

## How to Convert Your Glossary to Logseq with Ontology Features

This document shows practical examples of converting your metaverse glossary spreadsheet into Logseq pages with ontology edge labeling using properties.

## Example 1: Basic Term Entry

### From Spreadsheet:
| ID | Preferred Term | Definition | Domain | Maturity | Source |
|----|---------------|-----------|---------|----------|---------|
| 20017 | Avatar | Digital representation of a user | Interaction | mature | ETSI ARF 010 |

### To Logseq Page:

```markdown
# [[Avatar]]

## Properties
term-id:: 20017
preferred-term:: Avatar
definition:: Digital representation of a user in a virtual environment
maturity:: mature
source:: [[ETSI ARF 010]]

## Ontological Classification
domain:: [[ETSI Domain/Interaction]]
is-a:: [[Digital Representation]]
has-part:: [[Visual Model]], [[Animation Rig]], [[User Input Mapping]]

## Related Concepts
related-to:: [[Virtual World]], [[User Interface]], [[Identity]]
used-in:: [[Metaverse]], [[Virtual Reality]], [[Social VR]]

## Notes
Avatars serve as the primary means of self-representation and interaction within virtual environments.
```

## Example 2: Complex Term with Relationships

### From Spreadsheet:
| ID | Preferred Term | Definition | Domain | EWG Layer | Synonyms |
|----|---------------|-----------|---------|-----------|----------|
| 20049 | Digital Twin | Virtual representation synchronized with physical entity | Computation | Data Layer | Virtual Replica, Cyber Twin |

### To Logseq Page:

```markdown
# [[Digital Twin]]

## Core Properties
term-id:: 20049
preferred-term:: Digital Twin
definition:: Virtual representation of a physical entity that is synchronized in real-time with its physical counterpart
maturity:: mature
source:: [[ISO/IEC 23247]]

## Ontological Relationships
is-a:: [[Virtual Representation]]
subclass-of:: [[Cyber-Physical System]]
has-part::
  - [[Digital Model]]
  - [[Data Interface]]
  - [[Synchronization Engine]]
  - [[Analytics Module]]

requires::
  - [[IoT Sensors]]
  - [[Real-time Data Pipeline]]
  - [[3D Modeling]]

enables::
  - [[Predictive Maintenance]]
  - [[Remote Monitoring]]
  - [[Simulation]]
  - [[Optimization]]

## Classification
domain:: [[ETSI Domain/Computation and Intelligence]]
layer:: [[Data Layer]]
aspect:: [[Industrial]], [[Smart Cities]]

## Terminology
synonyms:: [[Virtual Replica]], [[Cyber Twin]], [[Digital Counterpart]]
variant-terms:: [[Device Shadow]], [[Virtual Prototype]]

## Standards & Sources
primary-source:: [[ISO/IEC 23247]]
also-defined-in:: [[IEEE]], [[ETSI]], [[Digital Twin Consortium]]
schema-org-type:: DigitalDocument

## Related Concepts
related-to::
  - [[Physical Asset]]
  - [[IoT Platform]]
  - [[Simulation]]
  - [[Metaverse]]
  - [[Extended Reality]]

## Use Cases
applications::
  - Manufacturing optimization
  - Healthcare patient modeling
  - Smart city infrastructure
  - Aerospace predictive maintenance
```

## Example 3: Hierarchical Concept Structure

```markdown
# [[Extended Reality]]

term-id:: 20060
preferred-term:: Extended Reality
abbreviation:: XR
definition:: Umbrella term encompassing virtual, augmented, and mixed reality technologies
maturity:: mature

## Hierarchical Structure
is-a:: [[Immersive Technology]]
has-subclass::
  - [[Virtual Reality]]
  - [[Augmented Reality]]
  - [[Mixed Reality]]

## Each Subclass (separate pages):

# [[Virtual Reality]]
is-a:: [[Extended Reality]]
abbreviation:: VR
has-part:: [[Head-Mounted Display]], [[Motion Tracking]], [[3D Audio]]

# [[Augmented Reality]]
is-a:: [[Extended Reality]]
abbreviation:: AR
has-part:: [[Reality Overlay]], [[Spatial Mapping]], [[Object Recognition]]

# [[Mixed Reality]]
is-a:: [[Extended Reality]]
abbreviation:: MR
combines:: [[Virtual Reality]], [[Augmented Reality]]
has-part:: [[Holographic Display]], [[Environment Understanding]]
```

## Example 4: Multi-Domain Term

```markdown
# [[Blockchain]]

term-id:: 20095
preferred-term:: Blockchain
definition:: Distributed ledger technology using cryptographic linking of data blocks
maturity:: mature
source:: [[ETSI]], [[W3C]]

## Multi-Domain Classification
domain:: [[ETSI Domain/Trust and Governance]], [[ETSI Domain/Infrastructure]]
layer:: [[Data Layer]], [[Security Layer]]

## Ontological Relationships
is-a:: [[Distributed Ledger]]
enables::
  - [[Decentralization]]
  - [[Immutability]]
  - [[Transparency]]
  - [[Smart Contracts]]

has-part::
  - [[Block]]
  - [[Hash Function]]
  - [[Consensus Mechanism]]
  - [[Distributed Network]]

## Metaverse Applications
used-in::
  - [[NFT Marketplace]]
  - [[Virtual Land Registry]]
  - [[Digital Asset Ownership]]
  - [[Decentralized Identity]]

## Technical Properties
consensus-types:: [[Proof of Work]], [[Proof of Stake]], [[Byzantine Fault Tolerance]]
characteristics:: distributed, immutable, transparent, trustless
```

## Query Examples for Your Glossary

### 1. Find All Terms in a Specific Domain

```clojure
#+BEGIN_QUERY
{:title "All Interaction Domain Terms"
 :query [:find (pull ?p [:block/name :block/properties])
         :where
         [?p :block/properties ?props]
         [(get ?props :domain) ?d]
         [(clojure.string/includes? ?d "Interaction")]]
}
#+END_QUERY
```

### 2. Find Mature Terms with Sources

```clojure
#+BEGIN_QUERY
{:title "Mature Terms from ETSI"
 :query [:find ?term ?definition ?source
         :where
         [?p :block/name ?term]
         [?p :block/properties ?props]
         [(get ?props :maturity) ?m]
         [(= ?m "mature")]
         [(get ?props :source) ?source]
         [(clojure.string/includes? ?source "ETSI")]
         [(get ?props :definition) ?definition]]
}
#+END_QUERY
```

### 3. Build Concept Hierarchy

```clojure
#+BEGIN_QUERY
{:title "Concept Hierarchy (is-a relationships)"
 :query [:find ?child ?parent
         :where
         [?p :block/properties ?props]
         [?p :block/name ?child]
         [(get ?props :is-a) ?parent]]
 :view (fn [results]
         [:div
          [:ul
           (for [[child parent] (sort-by second results)]
             [:li [:b parent] " ← " child])]])
}
#+END_QUERY
```

### 4. Find Terms by Synonym

```clojure
#+BEGIN_QUERY
{:title "Find term by synonym 'Virtual Replica'"
 :query [:find ?term ?preferred
         :where
         [?p :block/properties ?props]
         [?p :block/name ?term]
         [(get ?props :synonyms) ?syns]
         [(clojure.string/includes? ?syns "Virtual Replica")]
         [(get ?props :preferred-term) ?preferred]]
}
#+END_QUERY
```

### 5. Cross-Domain Terms

```clojure
#+BEGIN_QUERY
{:title "Terms spanning multiple domains"
 :query [:find ?term (count ?domain)
         :where
         [?p :block/name ?term]
         [?p :block/properties ?props]
         [(get ?props :domain) ?domains]
         [(re-seq #"\[\[.*?\]\]" ?domains) ?domain-list]
         [(count ?domain-list) ?domain]
         [(> ?domain 1)]]
}
#+END_QUERY
```

### 6. Technology Stack Query

```clojure
#+BEGIN_QUERY
{:title "What does Digital Twin require and enable?"
 :query [:find ?requirement ?capability
         :where
         [?dt :block/name "digital twin"]
         [?dt :block/properties ?props]
         [(get ?props :requires) ?requirement]
         [(get ?props :enables) ?capability]]
}
#+END_QUERY
```

## Workflow: Converting Your Spreadsheet

### Step 1: Create Page Template
Create a reusable template for glossary entries:

```markdown
## Template: Glossary Term

term-id:: 
preferred-term:: 
definition:: 
maturity:: 
source:: 

domain:: 
layer:: 
aspect:: 

is-a:: 
has-part:: 
requires:: 
enables:: 
related-to:: 

synonyms:: 
variant-terms:: 

notes::
```

### Step 2: Bulk Import Strategy

For bulk conversion, you could:

1. **Manual Entry** (best for small glossaries)
   - Create a page for each term
   - Apply the template
   - Fill in properties from spreadsheet

2. **Script-Assisted** (for large glossaries)
   - Export Excel to CSV
   - Write a Python/JavaScript script to generate markdown files
   - Import the generated files into Logseq

3. **Hybrid Approach** (recommended)
   - Script generates basic page structure with properties
   - Manually add ontological relationships (is-a, has-part, etc.)
   - Use queries to validate and enrich relationships

### Step 3: Define Your Ontology Schema

Create a master schema page:

```markdown
# Metaverse Ontology Schema

## Core Relationship Properties

### Taxonomic
- `is-a::` - direct parent class
- `subclass-of::` - broader classification
- `instance-of::` - instantiation

### Compositional
- `has-part::` - component relationships
- `consists-of::` - aggregation
- `contains::` - containment

### Dependency
- `requires::` - prerequisites
- `depends-on::` - dependencies
- `uses::` - utilization

### Capability
- `enables::` - capabilities provided
- `supports::` - support relationships
- `provides::` - provisions

### Association
- `related-to::` - general association
- `used-in::` - application contexts
- `implements::` - realization

## Metadata Properties

### Identification
- `term-id::` - unique identifier
- `preferred-term::` - canonical name
- `abbreviation::` - short form

### Documentation
- `definition::` - formal definition
- `notes::` - explanatory notes
- `example::` - usage examples

### Classification
- `domain::` - ETSI domain
- `layer::` - architectural layer
- `aspect::` - MSF aspect/vertical

### Provenance
- `source::` - authoritative source
- `primary-source::` - main reference
- `also-defined-in::` - additional sources

### Status
- `maturity::` - term maturity (draft/mature/deprecated)
- `version::` - specification version
- `status::` - standardization status

### Terminology
- `synonyms::` - equivalent terms
- `variant-terms::` - related variants
- `see-also::` - cross-references
```

## Advanced Pattern: Weighted Relationships

For more sophisticated ontologies, you can add weight/confidence scores:

```markdown
# [[Metaverse]]

## Strong Relationships (certainty: high)
is-a:: [[Virtual Environment]]
has-part:: [[Avatar]], [[Virtual World]], [[Digital Economy]]

## Moderate Relationships (certainty: medium)  
related-to:: [[Web3]]
  relationship-strength:: moderate
  
may-require:: [[VR Hardware]]
  dependency-type:: optional
  
## Emerging Relationships (certainty: low)
potentially-enables:: [[Parallel Economy]]
  maturity:: speculative
```

## Tips for Ontology Maintenance

### 1. Use Consistent Naming
- Prefer singular forms: `[[Avatar]]` not `[[Avatars]]`
- Use title case for concepts
- Create aliases for variants

### 2. Regular Validation Queries
Create queries to find:
- Terms without definitions
- Terms without domain classification
- Orphaned terms (no relationships)
- Circular relationships

### 3. Link Your Schema
Reference your schema page from term pages:

```markdown
schema-compliant:: [[Metaverse Ontology Schema]]
last-reviewed:: [[2025-01-15]]
```

### 4. Version Control
Track ontology evolution:

```markdown
# [[Avatar]]

version:: 2.1
changelog::
  - 2.1: Added has-part relationships for components
  - 2.0: Refined is-a relationship to Digital Representation
  - 1.0: Initial definition
```

## Conclusion

This property-based approach gives you:
- ✅ Structured ontology representation in plain markdown
- ✅ Powerful querying via Datalog
- ✅ Human-readable and machine-processable
- ✅ Incremental adoption (start simple, add complexity as needed)
- ✅ Compatible with standard markdown tools

Start with basic properties (term-id, definition, domain) and progressively add ontological relationships as your understanding of the domain matures.

=== owl_conversion_scripts.md ===
# Markdown to OWL Conversion Scripts

Templates for converting OWL-enhanced markdown to formal OWL ontologies for horned-owl validation.

---

## Python Converter (Using py-horned-owl)

```python
#!/usr/bin/env python3
"""
Convert Logseq markdown with OWL structures to OWL Functional Syntax

Requirements:
  pip install py-horned-owl pyyaml
"""

import re
from pathlib import Path
from typing import Dict, List, Optional
import pyhornedowl

class MarkdownOWLConverter:
    def __init__(self, base_iri: str = "https://metaverse-ontology.org/"):
        self.base_iri = base_iri
        self.onto = pyhornedowl.PyIndexedOntology()
        self.prefixes = {
            'mv': base_iri,
            'owl': 'http://www.w3.org/2002/07/owl#',
            'rdf': 'http://www.w3.org/1999/02/22-rdf-syntax-ns#',
            'rdfs': 'http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#',
            'xsd': 'http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#'
        }
        
    def parse_markdown_properties(self, file_path: Path) -> Dict[str, any]:
        """Extract properties from markdown file."""
        properties = {}
        current_section = None
        multiline_value = []
        in_multiline = False
        
        with open(file_path, 'r', encoding='utf-8') as f:
            for line in f:
                line = line.rstrip()
                
                # Section headers
                if line.startswith('##'):
                    current_section = line.replace('##', '').strip()
                    continue
                
                # Property lines (key:: value)
                match = re.match(r'^([a-zA-Z0-9-]+)::\s*(.*)$', line)
                if match:
                    key, value = match.groups()
                    
                    # Handle multiline start
                    if value.endswith('|'):
                        in_multiline = True
                        multiline_value = []
                        properties[key] = None  # Placeholder
                    else:
                        properties[key] = value.strip()
                elif in_multiline:
                    # Multiline content
                    if line.strip():
                        multiline_value.append(line)
                    else:
                        # End of multiline
                        in_multiline = False
                        # Find the key for this multiline value
                        for k, v in properties.items():
                            if v is None:
                                properties[k] = '
'.join(multiline_value)
                                break
                        multiline_value = []
        
        return properties
    
    def expand_iri(self, short_iri: str) -> str:
        """Expand prefixed IRI to full IRI."""
        if ':' in short_iri and not short_iri.startswith('http'):
            prefix, local = short_iri.split(':', 1)
            if prefix in self.prefixes:
                return self.prefixes[prefix] + local
        return short_iri
    
    def process_class(self, properties: Dict[str, any], file_name: str):
        """Process a class definition from markdown."""
        
        # Get IRI
        iri = properties.get('owl:iri')
        if not iri:
            # Generate IRI from filename
            class_name = file_name.replace('.md', '').replace(' ', '')
            iri = self.base_iri + class_name
        
        # Add class declaration
        self.onto.add_axiom(f"Declaration(Class({iri}))")
        
        # Add label
        if 'preferred-term' in properties:
            label = properties['preferred-term']
            self.onto.add_axiom(
                f'AnnotationAssertion(rdfs:label {iri} "{label}"@en)'
            )
        
        # Add definition
        if 'definition' in properties:
            definition = properties['definition'].replace('"', '\\"')
            self.onto.add_axiom(
                f'AnnotationAssertion(rdfs:comment {iri} "{definition}"@en)'
            )
        
        # Process SubClassOf from is-a property
        if 'is-a' in properties:
            parents = self.parse_entity_list(properties['is-a'])
            for parent in parents:
                parent_iri = self.expand_iri(parent)
                self.onto.add_axiom(f"SubClassOf({iri} {parent_iri})")
        
        # Process functional syntax block if present
        if 'owl:functional-syntax' in properties:
            functional_syntax = properties['owl:functional-syntax']
            for axiom in self.parse_functional_syntax_block(functional_syntax):
                try:
                    self.onto.add_axiom(axiom)
                except Exception as e:
                    print(f"Warning: Could not add axiom: {axiom}")
                    print(f"  Error: {e}")
    
    def process_object_property(self, properties: Dict[str, any], file_name: str):
        """Process an object property definition."""
        
        iri = properties.get('owl:iri')
        if not iri:
            prop_name = file_name.replace('.md', '').replace(' ', '').replace('-', '')
            iri = self.base_iri + prop_name
        
        # Declaration
        self.onto.add_axiom(f"Declaration(ObjectProperty({iri}))")
        
        # Characteristics
        if properties.get('owl:transitive') == 'true':
            self.onto.add_axiom(f"TransitiveObjectProperty({iri})")
        
        if properties.get('owl:reflexive') == 'true':
            self.onto.add_axiom(f"ReflexiveObjectProperty({iri})")
        
        if properties.get('owl:irreflexive') == 'true':
            self.onto.add_axiom(f"IrreflexiveObjectProperty({iri})")
        
        if properties.get('owl:symmetric') == 'true':
            self.onto.add_axiom(f"SymmetricObjectProperty({iri})")
        
        if properties.get('owl:asymmetric') == 'true':
            self.onto.add_axiom(f"AsymmetricObjectProperty({iri})")
        
        # Domain and Range
        if 'owl:domain' in properties:
            domain = self.expand_iri(properties['owl:domain'])
            self.onto.add_axiom(f"ObjectPropertyDomain({iri} {domain})")
        
        if 'owl:range' in properties:
            range_cls = self.expand_iri(properties['owl:range'])
            self.onto.add_axiom(f"ObjectPropertyRange({iri} {range_cls})")
        
        # Inverse
        if 'owl:inverse-of' in properties:
            inverse = self.expand_iri(properties['owl:inverse-of'])
            self.onto.add_axiom(f"InverseObjectProperties({iri} {inverse})")
    
    def process_data_property(self, properties: Dict[str, any], file_name: str):
        """Process a data property definition."""
        
        iri = properties.get('owl:iri')
        if not iri:
            prop_name = file_name.replace('.md', '').replace(' ', '').replace('-', '')
            iri = self.base_iri + prop_name
        
        # Declaration
        self.onto.add_axiom(f"Declaration(DataProperty({iri}))")
        
        # Functional
        if properties.get('owl:functional') == 'true':
            self.onto.add_axiom(f"FunctionalDataProperty({iri})")
        
        # Domain
        if 'owl:domain' in properties:
            domain = self.expand_iri(properties['owl:domain'])
            self.onto.add_axiom(f"DataPropertyDomain({iri} {domain})")
        
        # Range
        if 'owl:range' in properties:
            range_type = properties['owl:range']
            self.onto.add_axiom(f"DataPropertyRange({iri} {range_type})")
    
    def parse_entity_list(self, value: str) -> List[str]:
        """Parse comma-separated list of [[Entity]] references."""
        entities = []
        for match in re.finditer(r'\[\[([^\]]+)\]\]', value):
            entity = match.group(1)
            entities.append(entity.replace(' ', ''))
        return entities
    
    def parse_functional_syntax_block(self, block: str) -> List[str]:
        """Parse functional syntax block into individual axioms."""
        axioms = []
        lines = block.strip().split('
')
        current_axiom = []
        paren_depth = 0
        
        for line in lines:
            # Skip comments
            if line.strip().startswith('#'):
                continue
            
            if not line.strip():
                continue
            
            # Track parenthesis depth
            paren_depth += line.count('(') - line.count(')')
            current_axiom.append(line)
            
            # Complete axiom when parentheses balance
            if paren_depth == 0 and current_axiom:
                axiom = ' '.join(current_axiom).strip()
                if axiom:
                    axioms.append(axiom)
                current_axiom = []
        
        return axioms
    
    def convert_directory(self, input_dir: Path, output_file: Path):
        """Convert all markdown files in directory to OWL."""
        
        print(f"Converting {input_dir} to OWL...")
        
        # Process all markdown files
        for md_file in input_dir.glob('**/*.md'):
            print(f"  Processing {md_file.name}...")
            
            properties = self.parse_markdown_properties(md_file)
            
            # Determine entity type and process accordingly
            entity_type = properties.get('owl:entity-type', 'Class')
            
            if entity_type == 'Class':
                self.process_class(properties, md_file.name)
            elif entity_type == 'ObjectProperty':
                self.process_object_property(properties, md_file.name)
            elif entity_type == 'DataProperty':
                self.process_data_property(properties, md_file.name)
        
        # Save ontology
        print(f"
Saving to {output_file}...")
        self.onto.save_to_file(str(output_file), format='functional')
        
        print(f"
Conversion complete!")
        print(f"  Total axioms: {len(self.onto.get_axioms())}")
        print(f"  Total classes: {len(self.onto.get_classes())}")
    
    def validate(self) -> bool:
        """Validate the ontology for consistency."""
        print("
Validating ontology consistency...")
        is_consistent = self.onto.check_consistency()
        
        if is_consistent:
            print("✓ Ontology is consistent")
        else:
            print("✗ Ontology is inconsistent!")
        
        return is_consistent


def main():
    import argparse
    
    parser = argparse.ArgumentParser(
        description='Convert Logseq markdown with OWL structures to OWL Functional Syntax'
    )
    parser.add_argument(
        '--input',
        type=Path,
        required=True,
        help='Input directory containing markdown files'
    )
    parser.add_argument(
        '--output',
        type=Path,
        required=True,
        help='Output OWL file (functional syntax)'
    )
    parser.add_argument(
        '--base-iri',
        type=str,
        default='https://metaverse-ontology.org/',
        help='Base IRI for the ontology'
    )
    parser.add_argument(
        '--validate',
        action='store_true',
        help='Run consistency validation after conversion'
    )
    
    args = parser.parse_args()
    
    # Convert
    converter = MarkdownOWLConverter(base_iri=args.base_iri)
    converter.convert_directory(args.input, args.output)
    
    # Validate if requested
    if args.validate:
        is_consistent = converter.validate()
        if not is_consistent:
            exit(1)


if __name__ == '__main__':
    main()
```

### Usage

```bash
# Install dependencies
pip install py-horned-owl

# Convert markdown to OWL
python markdown_to_owl.py \
  --input ./logseq_pages/ \
  --output metaverse_ontology.ofn \
  --base-iri https://metaverse-ontology.org/ \
  --validate

# Validate with horned-bin
horned validate metaverse_ontology.ofn
```

---

## Rust Converter (Native Horned-Owl)

```rust
use horned_owl::model::*;
use horned_owl::ontology::set::SetOntology;
use horned_functional;
use std::collections::HashMap;
use std::fs;
use std::path::Path;

pub struct MarkdownOWLConverter {
    ontology: SetOntology<String>,
    base_iri: String,
}

impl MarkdownOWLConverter {
    pub fn new(base_iri: String) -> Self {
        Self {
            ontology: SetOntology::new(),
            base_iri,
        }
    }
    
    /// Parse markdown file and extract properties
    fn parse_markdown_properties(
        &self,
        content: &str
    ) -> HashMap<String, String> {
        let mut properties = HashMap::new();
        let mut in_multiline = false;
        let mut multiline_key = String::new();
        let mut multiline_content = Vec::new();
        
        for line in content.lines() {
            let line = line.trim();
            
            // Check for property pattern: key:: value
            if line.contains("::") && !line.starts_with('#') {
                if in_multiline {
                    // Save previous multiline
                    properties.insert(
                        multiline_key.clone(),
                        multiline_content.join("
")
                    );
                    in_multiline = false;
                    multiline_content.clear();
                }
                
                let parts: Vec<&str> = line.splitn(2, "::").collect();
                if parts.len() == 2 {
                    let key = parts[0].trim().to_string();
                    let value = parts[1].trim();
                    
                    if value.ends_with('|') {
                        // Start multiline
                        in_multiline = true;
                        multiline_key = key;
                    } else {
                        properties.insert(key, value.to_string());
                    }
                }
            } else if in_multiline && !line.is_empty() {
                multiline_content.push(line.to_string());
            }
        }
        
        properties
    }
    
    /// Convert class definition to OWL
    fn process_class(
        &mut self,
        properties: &HashMap<String, String>,
        file_name: &str
    ) {
        // Get IRI
        let iri = properties
            .get("owl:iri")
            .cloned()
            .unwrap_or_else(|| {
                let class_name = file_name
                    .replace(".md", "")
                    .replace(" ", "");
                format!("{}{}", self.base_iri, class_name)
            });
        
        let class = Class(IRI(iri.clone()));
        
        // Add declaration
        self.ontology.insert(Declaration::Class(class.clone()));
        
        // Add label annotation
        if let Some(label) = properties.get("preferred-term") {
            let annotation = Annotation {
                ap: AnnotationProperty(IRI("http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#label".into())),
                av: AnnotationValue::Literal(Literal::Simple {
                    literal: label.clone(),
                }),
            };
            
            self.ontology.insert(AnnotationAssertion {
                subject: iri.clone().into(),
                ann: annotation,
            });
        }
        
        // Process SubClassOf from is-a
        if let Some(is_a) = properties.get("is-a") {
            for parent in self.parse_entity_list(is_a) {
                let parent_class = Class(IRI(parent));
                self.ontology.insert(SubClassOf {
                    sub: ClassExpression::Class(class.clone()),
                    sup: ClassExpression::Class(parent_class),
                });
            }
        }
        
        // Process functional syntax if present
        if let Some(func_syntax) = properties.get("owl:functional-syntax") {
            // Parse and add axioms from functional syntax block
            // This would use horned-functional to parse
            if let Ok((parsed_onto, _)) = horned_functional::from_str::<SetOntology<String>, String>(func_syntax) {
                for axiom in parsed_onto.axioms() {
                    self.ontology.insert(axiom.clone());
                }
            }
        }
    }
    
    /// Parse entity list from [[Entity1]], [[Entity2]] format
    fn parse_entity_list(&self, value: &str) -> Vec<String> {
        let re = regex::Regex::new(r"\[\[([^\]]+)\]\]").unwrap();
        re.captures_iter(value)
            .map(|cap| {
                let entity = &cap[1];
                format!("{}{}", self.base_iri, entity.replace(" ", ""))
            })
            .collect()
    }
    
    /// Convert entire directory of markdown files
    pub fn convert_directory(
        &mut self,
        input_dir: &Path
    ) -> Result<(), Box<dyn std::error::Error>> {
        for entry in fs::read_dir(input_dir)? {
            let entry = entry?;
            let path = entry.path();
            
            if path.extension().and_then(|s| s.to_str()) == Some("md") {
                let content = fs::read_to_string(&path)?;
                let properties = self.parse_markdown_properties(&content);
                
                let entity_type = properties
                    .get("owl:entity-type")
                    .map(|s| s.as_str())
                    .unwrap_or("Class");
                
                match entity_type {
                    "Class" => {
                        self.process_class(
                            &properties,
                            path.file_name()
                                .and_then(|s| s.to_str())
                                .unwrap_or("Unknown")
                        );
                    }
                    "ObjectProperty" => {
                        // Process object property
                        // Similar to process_class
                    }
                    "DataProperty" => {
                        // Process data property
                    }
                    _ => {}
                }
            }
        }
        
        Ok(())
    }
    
    /// Save ontology to file in functional syntax
    pub fn save_functional_syntax(
        &self,
        output_path: &Path
    ) -> Result<(), Box<dyn std::error::Error>> {
        let functional_syntax = horned_functional::to_string(&self.ontology)?;
        fs::write(output_path, functional_syntax)?;
        Ok(())
    }
}

fn main() -> Result<(), Box<dyn std::error::Error>> {
    let args: Vec<String> = std::env::args().collect();
    
    if args.len() < 3 {
        eprintln!("Usage: {} <input_dir> <output_file>", args[0]);
        std::process::exit(1);
    }
    
    let input_dir = Path::new(&args[1]);
    let output_file = Path::new(&args[2]);
    
    println!("Converting {} to OWL...", input_dir.display());
    
    let mut converter = MarkdownOWLConverter::new(
        "https://metaverse-ontology.org/".to_string()
    );
    
    converter.convert_directory(input_dir)?;
    converter.save_functional_syntax(output_file)?;
    
    println!("Conversion complete! Saved to {}", output_file.display());
    
    Ok(())
}
```

### Cargo.toml

```toml
[package]
name = "markdown-owl-converter"
version = "0.1.0"
edition = "2021"

[dependencies]
horned-owl = "1.0"
horned-functional = "0.4"
regex = "1.10"
```

### Usage

```bash
# Build
cargo build --release

# Convert
./target/release/markdown-owl-converter \
  ./logseq_pages/ \
  metaverse_ontology.ofn

# Validate with horned-bin
horned validate metaverse_ontology.ofn
```

---

## Validation Script

```bash
#!/bin/bash
# validate_ontology.sh

set -e

INPUT_DIR="$1"
OUTPUT_FILE="metaverse_ontology.ofn"

echo "=== Metaverse Ontology Validation Pipeline ==="
echo

echo "Step 1: Converting markdown to OWL..."
python markdown_to_owl.py \
  --input "$INPUT_DIR" \
  --output "$OUTPUT_FILE" \
  --validate

echo
echo "Step 2: Validating with horned-bin..."
horned validate "$OUTPUT_FILE"

echo
echo "Step 3: Checking profile compliance..."
horned profile "$OUTPUT_FILE"

echo
echo "Step 4: Computing metrics..."
horned metrics "$OUTPUT_FILE"

echo
echo "=== Validation Complete ==="
```

---

## CI/CD Integration

### GitHub Actions

```yaml
name: Ontology Validation

on:
  push:
    paths:
      - 'logseq_pages/**'
  pull_request:
    paths:
      - 'logseq_pages/**'

jobs:
  validate:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v3
      
      - name: Setup Python
        uses: actions/setup-python@v4
        with:
          python-version: '3.11'
      
      - name: Install dependencies
        run: |
          pip install py-horned-owl
      
      - name: Convert to OWL
        run: |
          python scripts/markdown_to_owl.py \
            --input ./logseq_pages/ \
            --output metaverse_ontology.ofn \
            --validate
      
      - name: Upload ontology artifact
        uses: actions/upload-artifact@v3
        with:
          name: ontology
          path: metaverse_ontology.ofn
      
      - name: Validate consistency
        run: |
          # Check if ontology is consistent
          # Fail CI if inconsistent
          if ! python -c "import pyhornedowl; onto = pyhornedowl.open_ontology('metaverse_ontology.ofn'); assert onto.check_consistency()"; then
            echo "❌ Ontology is inconsistent!"
            exit 1
          fi
          echo "✅ Ontology is consistent"
```

---

## Next Steps

1. **Choose your approach** - Python (easier) or Rust (faster)
2. **Test on a few files** - Start with 5-10 terms
3. **Iterate on conversion** - Refine parsing logic
4. **Validate incrementally** - Fix issues as they arise
5. **Automate** - Add to CI/CD pipeline

These scripts provide a starting point for converting your OWL-enhanced markdown to formal OWL ontologies that horned-owl can validate! 🚀

=== owl_enhanced_examples.md ===
# Updated Term Examples with OWL Validation Support

These examples show how to enhance your existing Logseq pages with OWL structures for horned-owl validation.

---

## Example 1: Avatar (With OWL Structures)

```markdown
# [[Avatar]]

## OWL Ontology Metadata
owl:iri:: https://metaverse-ontology.org/Avatar
owl:entity-type:: Class
owl:declared-in:: MetaverseOntology
owl:version:: 1.0

## Core Properties
term-id:: 20067
preferred-term:: Avatar
definition:: Digital representation of a person or agent used to interact within a virtual environment
maturity:: mature
source:: [[ACM + Web3D HAnim]]

## Classification
domain:: [[ETSI Domain/Interaction]]
layer:: [[User Experience Layer]]
aspect:: [[Visualization]], [[Social Interaction]]

## Ontological Relationships
is-a:: [[Digital Representation]]
has-part:: [[Visual Model]], [[Animation Rig]], [[Texture Maps]]
requires:: [[3D Rendering Engine]], [[User Input Controller]]
enables:: [[User Embodiment]], [[Social Presence]]
related-to:: [[Virtual World]], [[User Identity]]

## OWL Axioms

### Declarations
owl:declaration:: Declaration(Class(mv:Avatar))

### SubClassOf Axioms
owl:subclass::
  - mv:Avatar ⊑ mv:DigitalRepresentation
  - mv:Avatar ⊑ mv:UserInterface
  - mv:Avatar ⊑ ∃hasPart.mv:VisualModel
  - mv:Avatar ⊑ ∃hasPart.mv:AnimationRig
  - mv:Avatar ⊑ ∃requires.mv:RenderingEngine

### Necessary Conditions (Restrictions)
owl:restrictions::
  - ObjectSomeValuesFrom(mv:hasPart mv:VisualModel)
  - ObjectSomeValuesFrom(mv:requires mv:RenderingEngine)
  - ObjectMinCardinality(1 mv:hasPart)
  - ObjectExactCardinality(1 mv:representsUser mv:Person)

### Disjoint With
owl:disjoint-with::
  - mv:PhysicalObject
  - mv:RealWorldEntity

## OWL Functional Syntax (For Export)
owl:functional-syntax:: |
  # Entity Declaration
  Declaration(Class(mv:Avatar))
  
  # Basic Subsumption
  SubClassOf(mv:Avatar mv:DigitalRepresentation)
  SubClassOf(mv:Avatar mv:UserInterface)
  
  # Property Restrictions - Has Parts
  SubClassOf(
    mv:Avatar
    ObjectSomeValuesFrom(mv:hasPart mv:VisualModel)
  )
  SubClassOf(
    mv:Avatar
    ObjectSomeValuesFrom(mv:hasPart mv:AnimationRig)
  )
  SubClassOf(
    mv:Avatar
    ObjectSomeValuesFrom(mv:hasPart mv:TextureMaps)
  )
  
  # Property Restrictions - Requirements
  SubClassOf(
    mv:Avatar
    ObjectSomeValuesFrom(mv:requires mv:RenderingEngine)
  )
  SubClassOf(
    mv:Avatar
    ObjectSomeValuesFrom(mv:requires mv:UserInputController)
  )
  
  # Property Restrictions - Capabilities
  SubClassOf(
    mv:Avatar
    ObjectSomeValuesFrom(mv:enables mv:UserEmbodiment)
  )
  SubClassOf(
    mv:Avatar
    ObjectSomeValuesFrom(mv:enables mv:SocialPresence)
  )
  
  # Cardinality Constraints
  SubClassOf(
    mv:Avatar
    ObjectMinCardinality(1 mv:hasPart)
  )
  SubClassOf(
    mv:Avatar
    ObjectExactCardinality(1 mv:representsUser mv:Person)
  )
  
  # Disjointness
  DisjointClasses(mv:Avatar mv:PhysicalObject)
  
  # Annotations
  AnnotationAssertion(
    rdfs:label
    mv:Avatar
    "Avatar"@en
  )
  AnnotationAssertion(
    rdfs:comment
    mv:Avatar
    "Digital representation of a person or agent used to interact within a virtual environment"@en
  )
  AnnotationAssertion(
    mv:termId
    mv:Avatar
    "20067"^^xsd:integer
  )
  AnnotationAssertion(
    mv:maturity
    mv:Avatar
    "mature"^^xsd:string
  )

## Validation Configuration
owl:validation-profile:: OWL2-DL
owl:expected-satisfiable:: true
owl:consistency-check:: required

## Terminology
synonyms:: [[Virtual Persona]], [[Digital Identity]]
```

---

## Example 2: Digital Twin (Complex Constraints)

```markdown
# [[Digital Twin]]

## OWL Ontology Metadata
owl:iri:: https://metaverse-ontology.org/DigitalTwin
owl:entity-type:: Class
owl:declared-in:: MetaverseOntology

## Core Properties
term-id:: 20213
preferred-term:: Digital Twin
definition:: Virtual representation of a physical entity that is continuously synchronized with real-time data from its physical counterpart
maturity:: mature
source:: [[ISO/IEC 23247]]

## Classification
domain:: [[ETSI Domain/Computation and Intelligence]]
layer:: [[Data Layer]]

## Ontological Relationships
is-a:: [[Virtual Representation]]
subclass-of:: [[Cyber-Physical System]]
has-part:: [[Digital Model]], [[Synchronization Engine]], [[Analytics Module]]
requires:: [[IoT Sensors]], [[Real-time Data Pipeline]]
enables:: [[Predictive Maintenance]], [[Remote Monitoring]]
binds-to:: [[Physical Asset]]

## OWL Axioms

### Complex Class Expression
owl:equivalent-to::
  VirtualRepresentation ⊓ 
  ∃bindsTo.PhysicalAsset ⊓ 
  ∃hasPart.SynchronizationEngine ⊓
  ∃receives.RealTimeData

## OWL Functional Syntax
owl:functional-syntax:: |
  Declaration(Class(mv:DigitalTwin))
  
  # Multiple Inheritance
  SubClassOf(mv:DigitalTwin mv:VirtualRepresentation)
  SubClassOf(mv:DigitalTwin mv:CyberPhysicalSystem)
  
  # Equivalence (Necessary and Sufficient)
  EquivalentClasses(
    mv:DigitalTwin
    ObjectIntersectionOf(
      mv:VirtualRepresentation
      ObjectSomeValuesFrom(mv:bindsTo mv:PhysicalAsset)
      ObjectSomeValuesFrom(mv:hasPart mv:SynchronizationEngine)
      ObjectSomeValuesFrom(mv:receives mv:RealTimeData)
    )
  )
  
  # Required Components
  SubClassOf(
    mv:DigitalTwin
    ObjectSomeValuesFrom(mv:hasPart mv:DigitalModel)
  )
  SubClassOf(
    mv:DigitalTwin
    ObjectSomeValuesFrom(mv:hasPart mv:SynchronizationEngine)
  )
  SubClassOf(
    mv:DigitalTwin
    ObjectSomeValuesFrom(mv:hasPart mv:AnalyticsModule)
  )
  
  # Technical Requirements
  SubClassOf(
    mv:DigitalTwin
    ObjectSomeValuesFrom(mv:requires mv:IoTSensors)
  )
  SubClassOf(
    mv:DigitalTwin
    ObjectSomeValuesFrom(mv:requires mv:RealTimeDataPipeline)
  )
  
  # Cardinality: Must bind to exactly one physical asset
  SubClassOf(
    mv:DigitalTwin
    ObjectExactCardinality(1 mv:bindsTo mv:PhysicalAsset)
  )
  
  # Cardinality: Must have at least one synchronization engine
  SubClassOf(
    mv:DigitalTwin
    ObjectMinCardinality(1 mv:hasPart mv:SynchronizationEngine)
  )
  
  # Universal Quantification: All data received must be real-time
  SubClassOf(
    mv:DigitalTwin
    ObjectAllValuesFrom(mv:receives mv:RealTimeData)
  )

## Terminology
synonyms:: [[Virtual Replica]], [[Cyber Twin]]
```

---

## Example 3: Object Property Definition (has-part)

```markdown
# Object Property: has-part

## OWL Ontology Metadata
owl:iri:: https://metaverse-ontology.org/hasPart
owl:entity-type:: ObjectProperty
owl:declared-in:: MetaverseOntology

## Property Characteristics
owl:transitive:: true
owl:irreflexive:: true
owl:asymmetric:: true

## Domain and Range
owl:domain:: mv:CompositeEntity
owl:range:: mv:Component

## Inverse Property
owl:inverse-of:: isPartOf

## Property Chain
owl:property-chain:: hasPart ∘ hasPart ⊑ hasPart

## OWL Functional Syntax
owl:functional-syntax:: |
  # Declaration
  Declaration(ObjectProperty(mv:hasPart))
  
  # Characteristics
  TransitiveObjectProperty(mv:hasPart)
  IrreflexiveObjectProperty(mv:hasPart)
  AsymmetricObjectProperty(mv:hasPart)
  
  # Domain and Range
  ObjectPropertyDomain(mv:hasPart mv:CompositeEntity)
  ObjectPropertyRange(mv:hasPart mv:Component)
  
  # Inverse
  InverseObjectProperties(mv:hasPart mv:isPartOf)
  
  # Property Chain (Transitivity)
  SubObjectPropertyOf(
    ObjectPropertyChain(mv:hasPart mv:hasPart)
    mv:hasPart
  )
  
  # Annotations
  AnnotationAssertion(
    rdfs:label
    mv:hasPart
    "has part"@en
  )
  AnnotationAssertion(
    rdfs:comment
    mv:hasPart
    "Relates a composite entity to its constituent components"@en
  )

## Usage Examples
example-usage::
  - VirtualWorld hasPart Avatar
  - Avatar hasPart VisualModel
  - Therefore: VirtualWorld hasPart VisualModel (by transitivity)

## Notes
This property represents mereological composition relationships. It is transitive (if A has-part B and B has-part C, then A has-part C), irreflexive (nothing is a part of itself), and asymmetric (if A has-part B, then B cannot have-part A).
```

---

## Example 4: Data Property Definition (term-id)

```markdown
# Data Property: term-id

## OWL Ontology Metadata
owl:iri:: https://metaverse-ontology.org/termId
owl:entity-type:: DataProperty
owl:declared-in:: MetaverseOntology

## Property Characteristics
owl:functional:: true

## Domain and Range
owl:domain:: mv:Concept
owl:range:: xsd:integer

## Constraints
owl:min-inclusive:: 20000
owl:max-inclusive:: 99999

## OWL Functional Syntax
owl:functional-syntax:: |
  # Declaration
  Declaration(DataProperty(mv:termId))
  
  # Functional (each concept has at most one term ID)
  FunctionalDataProperty(mv:termId)
  
  # Domain and Range
  DataPropertyDomain(mv:termId mv:Concept)
  DataPropertyRange(mv:termId xsd:integer)
  
  # Range Restriction (between 20000 and 99999)
  DataPropertyRange(
    mv:termId
    DatatypeRestriction(
      xsd:integer
      xsd:minInclusive "20000"^^xsd:integer
      xsd:maxInclusive "99999"^^xsd:integer
    )
  )
  
  # Annotations
  AnnotationAssertion(
    rdfs:label
    mv:termId
    "term identifier"@en
  )
  AnnotationAssertion(
    rdfs:comment
    mv:termId
    "Unique numeric identifier for a glossary term"@en
  )

## Usage
This property assigns a unique integer identifier to each concept in the glossary. The identifier is functional (each concept has exactly one ID) and must be in the range [20000, 99999].
```

---

## Example 5: Ontology Header File

```markdown
# Metaverse Ontology

## OWL Ontology Declaration
owl:ontology-iri:: https://metaverse-ontology.org/
owl:version-iri:: https://metaverse-ontology.org/v1.0
owl:ontology-version:: 1.0.0

## Prefixes
prefix:mv:: https://metaverse-ontology.org/
prefix:etsi:: https://etsi.org/ontology/
prefix:iso:: https://iso.org/ontology/
prefix:owl:: http://www.w3.org/2002/07/owl#
prefix:rdf:: http://www.w3.org/1999/02/22-rdf-syntax-ns#
prefix:rdfs:: http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#
prefix:xsd:: http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#
prefix:dc:: http://purl.org/dc/elements/1.1/

## Ontology Metadata
rdfs:label:: "Metaverse Ontology"@en
rdfs:comment:: "A formal ontology for metaverse concepts, technologies, and terminology"@en
dc:creator:: "Metaverse Ontology Working Group"
dc:contributor:: "ETSI, ISO, MSF"
dc:date:: "2025-01-15"
dc:description:: "Comprehensive ontology covering metaverse architecture, components, and standards"
owl:versionInfo:: "1.0"

## Imports
owl:imports::
  - https://www.w3.org/2002/07/owl
  - https://etsi.org/ontology/arf010

## OWL Functional Syntax
owl:functional-syntax:: |
  Prefix(:=<https://metaverse-ontology.org/>)
  Prefix(owl:=<http://www.w3.org/2002/07/owl#>)
  Prefix(rdf:=<http://www.w3.org/1999/02/22-rdf-syntax-ns#>)
  Prefix(rdfs:=<http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#>)
  Prefix(xsd:=<http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#>)
  
  Ontology(<https://metaverse-ontology.org/>
    <https://metaverse-ontology.org/v1.0>
    
    Import(<https://www.w3.org/2002/07/owl>)
    
    Annotation(rdfs:label "Metaverse Ontology"@en)
    Annotation(rdfs:comment "A formal ontology for metaverse concepts"@en)
    Annotation(owl:versionInfo "1.0")
    
    # Global Disjoint Classes
    DisjointClasses(mv:PhysicalEntity mv:VirtualEntity)
    DisjointClasses(mv:Hardware mv:Software mv:Data)
    DisjointClasses(mv:User mv:System mv:Agent)
    
    # Top-level Class Hierarchy
    Declaration(Class(mv:Entity))
    Declaration(Class(mv:PhysicalEntity))
    Declaration(Class(mv:VirtualEntity))
    
    SubClassOf(mv:PhysicalEntity mv:Entity)
    SubClassOf(mv:VirtualEntity mv:Entity)
    
    # Transitive Properties
    Declaration(ObjectProperty(mv:hasPart))
    Declaration(ObjectProperty(mv:isPartOf))
    Declaration(ObjectProperty(mv:subClassOf))
    
    TransitiveObjectProperty(mv:hasPart)
    TransitiveObjectProperty(mv:isPartOf)
    TransitiveObjectProperty(mv:subClassOf)
    
    InverseObjectProperties(mv:hasPart mv:isPartOf)
  )

## Validation Profile
owl:profile:: OWL2-DL
owl:expressivity:: ALCHIQ(D)
owl:consistency-required:: true
owl:coherence-required:: true

## Statistics
total-classes:: 229
total-object-properties:: 15
total-data-properties:: 8
total-annotation-properties:: 5
total-axioms:: ~2000 (estimated)
```

## Conversion Notes

### From Existing Logseq to OWL-Enhanced

1. **Keep all existing content** - Nothing is removed
2. **Add OWL sections** - New metadata blocks
3. **Add functional syntax** - Machine-readable export format
4. **Define properties once** - Reference in PropertySchema.md
5. **Validate incrementally** - Add OWL structures page by page

### Migration Strategy

```markdown
# Phase 1: Add IRIs (All Pages)
owl:iri:: https://metaverse-ontology.org/TermName
owl:entity-type:: Class

# Phase 2: Add Functional Syntax (Key Terms)
owl:functional-syntax:: |
  Declaration(Class(mv:TermName))
  SubClassOf(mv:TermName mv:ParentClass)

# Phase 3: Add Full Axioms (Critical Terms)
owl:restrictions::
  - ObjectSomeValuesFrom(mv:hasPart mv:Component)
  - ObjectMinCardinality(1 mv:requires)

# Phase 4: Complete All Terms
# + Validation
# + Export
# + Reasoning
```

These enhanced examples maintain full backward compatibility with your Logseq workflow while adding the formal structures needed for OWL validation! 🎯

=== owl_validation_engineering.md ===
# Engineering Markdown for OWL Validation with Horned-Owl

## Overview

To validate your metaverse glossary ontology using the **horned-owl** Rust crate, you need to add specific OWL 2-compliant structures to your markdown that can be exported to OWL Functional Syntax or RDF/XML for validation.

## What is Horned-Owl?

Horned-OWL is a library for processing and manipulating documents written using the Web Ontology Language (OWL), extending the Rust ecosystem for the Semantic Web. It provides support for OWL 2 language specification and can handle ontologies with millions of terms, showing 20x-40x speedup compared to competing implementations.

## Critical OWL Requirements for Validation

### 1. Entity Declarations

Each IRI used in an OWL 2 ontology must be declared, associating the IRI with an entity type (class, datatype, object property, data property, annotation property, individual, or combination thereof).

**What to Add to Markdown:**

```markdown
# [[Avatar]]

## OWL Declarations
owl:entity-type:: Class
owl:iri:: https://metaverse-ontology.org/Avatar
owl:declared-in:: MetaverseOntology

## Alternative: Compact Form
owl:Declaration:: Class(https://metaverse-ontology.org/Avatar)
```

### 2. Explicit Type Distinctions

OWL parsers need to know whether an IRI is an object property, data property, class, or datatype to disambiguate axioms.

**Property Type Declarations:**

```markdown
# Property Declarations

## Object Properties (link entities to entities)
is-a::
  owl:type:: ObjectProperty
  owl:iri:: https://metaverse-ontology.org/isA
  
has-part::
  owl:type:: ObjectProperty
  owl:iri:: https://metaverse-ontology.org/hasPart

## Data Properties (link entities to literal values)
term-id::
  owl:type:: DataProperty
  owl:iri:: https://metaverse-ontology.org/termId
  owl:range:: xsd:integer

definition::
  owl:type:: DataProperty  
  owl:iri:: https://metaverse-ontology.org/definition
  owl:range:: xsd:string

## Annotation Properties (metadata about ontology)
source::
  owl:type:: AnnotationProperty
  owl:iri:: https://metaverse-ontology.org/source
```

### 3. IRI Namespaces and Prefixes

**Add Namespace Declarations:**

```markdown
# Ontology Header

## Prefixes
prefix:mv:: https://metaverse-ontology.org/
prefix:etsi:: https://etsi.org/ontology/
prefix:owl:: http://www.w3.org/2002/07/owl#
prefix:rdf:: http://www.w3.org/1999/02/22-rdf-syntax-ns#
prefix:rdfs:: http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#
prefix:xsd:: http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#

## Ontology IRI
ontology:iri:: https://metaverse-ontology.org/
ontology:version:: https://metaverse-ontology.org/v1.0
```

### 4. Formal Axiom Structures

OWL 2 uses formal axioms like SubClassOf, EquivalentClasses, DisjointClasses to establish relationships between class expressions.

**Add Axiom Blocks:**

```markdown
# [[Avatar]]

## OWL Axioms

### SubClassOf Axioms
owl:SubClassOf::
  - Avatar ⊑ DigitalRepresentation
  - Avatar ⊑ UserInterface

### Functional Syntax (for export)
owl:axiom:: SubClassOf(mv:Avatar mv:DigitalRepresentation)
owl:axiom:: SubClassOf(mv:Avatar mv:UserInterface)

### Property Restrictions
owl:axiom:: SubClassOf(
  mv:Avatar
  ObjectSomeValuesFrom(mv:hasPart mv:VisualModel)
)

### Cardinality Restrictions
owl:axiom:: SubClassOf(
  mv:Avatar
  ObjectExactCardinality(1 mv:hasUser mv:Person)
)
```

### 5. Property Characteristics

**Add Property Metadata:**

```markdown
# Object Property: has-part

## OWL Property Characteristics
owl:type:: ObjectProperty
owl:transitive:: true
owl:irreflexive:: true

## Domain and Range
owl:domain:: PhysicalEntity ∪ VirtualEntity
owl:range:: Component

## Property Chain (for composition)
owl:property-chain:: hasPart ∘ hasPart ⊑ hasPart

## Functional Syntax
owl:axiom:: Declaration(ObjectProperty(mv:hasPart))
owl:axiom:: TransitiveObjectProperty(mv:hasPart)
owl:axiom:: IrreflexiveObjectProperty(mv:hasPart)
owl:axiom:: ObjectPropertyDomain(mv:hasPart mv:PhysicalEntity)
owl:axiom:: ObjectPropertyRange(mv:hasPart mv:Component)
```

### 6. Logical Constraints

**Add Restrictions and Constraints:**

```markdown
# [[Virtual World]]

## OWL Constraints

### Necessary Conditions (must have)
owl:necessary::
  - ObjectSomeValuesFrom(mv:hasPart mv:Avatar)
  - ObjectSomeValuesFrom(mv:requires mv:RenderingEngine)
  - ObjectMinCardinality(1 mv:hasUser)

### Sufficient Conditions (if has, then is)
owl:sufficient::
  - hasAvatars ∧ hasPersistence ∧ has3DEnvironment → VirtualWorld

### Disjointness
owl:disjoint-with::
  - PhysicalWorld
  - AugmentedReality

### Equivalence
owl:equivalent-to::
  - VirtualEnvironment ∧ MultiUser ∧ Persistent

## Functional Syntax
owl:axiom:: EquivalentClasses(
  mv:VirtualWorld
  ObjectIntersectionOf(
    mv:VirtualEnvironment
    ObjectSomeValuesFrom(mv:supports mv:MultiUser)
    ObjectSomeValuesFrom(mv:hasProperty mv:Persistence)
  )
)
```

### 7. Individual Instances (Optional)

**If your ontology includes specific instances:**

```markdown
# [[MetaQuest3]]

## OWL Individual
owl:type:: NamedIndividual
owl:class-assertion:: VRHeadset

## Property Assertions
owl:property-assertion::
  - manufacturer: Meta
  - releaseDate: "2023-10-10"^^xsd:date
  - supports: HandTracking
  - supports: PassthroughAR

## Functional Syntax
owl:axiom:: Declaration(NamedIndividual(mv:MetaQuest3))
owl:axiom:: ClassAssertion(mv:VRHeadset mv:MetaQuest3)
owl:axiom:: ObjectPropertyAssertion(mv:supports mv:MetaQuest3 mv:HandTracking)
```

## Recommended Markdown Structure

### Complete Term Template

```markdown
# [[TermName]]

## Ontology Metadata (NEW)
owl:iri:: https://metaverse-ontology.org/TermName
owl:entity-type:: Class
owl:declared-in:: MetaverseOntology
owl:version:: 1.0

## Core Properties (EXISTING)
term-id:: 20067
preferred-term:: TermName
definition:: Formal definition here
maturity:: mature
source:: [[Source]]

## Classification (EXISTING)
domain:: [[ETSI Domain/X]]
layer:: [[Y]]

## Ontological Relationships (EXISTING - keep as-is)
is-a:: [[ParentClass]]
has-part:: [[Component1]], [[Component2]]
requires:: [[Dependency]]
enables:: [[Capability]]

## OWL Axioms (NEW - formal export)
owl:subclass-axioms::
  - SubClassOf(mv:TermName mv:ParentClass)
  - SubClassOf(mv:TermName ObjectSomeValuesFrom(mv:hasPart mv:Component1))
  - SubClassOf(mv:TermName ObjectSomeValuesFrom(mv:hasPart mv:Component2))

owl:property-axioms::
  - ObjectPropertyDomain(mv:requires mv:TermName)
  - ObjectPropertyRange(mv:requires mv:Dependency)

owl:restrictions::
  - ObjectMinCardinality(1 mv:hasPart mv:Component1)
  - ObjectSomeValuesFrom(mv:enables mv:Capability)

## Validation Rules (NEW - for horned-owl)
owl:validation::
  - check-consistency: true
  - check-coherence: true
  - profile: OWL2-DL
  - expected-satisfiable: true

## Export Format (NEW - preferred syntax)
owl:functional-syntax:: |
  Declaration(Class(mv:TermName))
  SubClassOf(mv:TermName mv:ParentClass)
  SubClassOf(
    mv:TermName 
    ObjectSomeValuesFrom(mv:hasPart mv:Component1)
  )
  
  AnnotationAssertion(
    rdfs:label 
    mv:TermName 
    "TermName"^^xsd:string
  )

## Terminology (EXISTING)
synonyms:: [[Alt1]], [[Alt2]]
```

### Ontology-Level Metadata File

Create a separate `MetaverseOntology.md` file:

```markdown
# Metaverse Ontology

## OWL Ontology Declaration
owl:ontology-iri:: https://metaverse-ontology.org/
owl:version-iri:: https://metaverse-ontology.org/v1.0
owl:ontology-version:: 1.0.0

## Imports
owl:imports::
  - http://www.w3.org/2002/07/owl
  - https://etsi.org/ontology/arf010

## Prefixes
prefix:mv:: https://metaverse-ontology.org/
prefix:etsi:: https://etsi.org/ontology/
prefix:owl:: http://www.w3.org/2002/07/owl#
prefix:rdf:: http://www.w3.org/1999/02/22-rdf-syntax-ns#
prefix:rdfs:: http://www.w3.org/2000/01/rdf-schema#
prefix:xsd:: http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema#

## Ontology Annotations
rdfs:label:: "Metaverse Ontology"
rdfs:comment:: "An ontology for metaverse concepts and terminology"
dc:creator:: "Ontology Working Group"
dc:date:: "2025-01-15"
owl:versionInfo:: "1.0"

## Global Axioms

### Disjoint Classes
owl:disjoint-classes::
  - [PhysicalEntity, VirtualEntity]
  - [Hardware, Software]
  - [User, System]

### Property Hierarchies
owl:sub-properties::
  - containsPart ⊑ hasPart
  - directlyContains ⊑ containsPart

### Transitive Properties
owl:transitive-properties::
  - hasPart
  - subClassOf
  - isPartOf

## Validation Configuration
owl:profile:: OWL2-DL
owl:consistency-checks:: true
owl:coherence-checks:: true
```

## Property Schema File

Create `PropertySchema.md`:

```markdown
# Property Schema

## Object Properties

### is-a
owl:iri:: https://metaverse-ontology.org/isA
owl:type:: ObjectProperty
owl:equivalent:: rdfs:subClassOf
owl:transitive:: true
owl:reflexive:: true

### has-part
owl:iri:: https://metaverse-ontology.org/hasPart
owl:type:: ObjectProperty
owl:transitive:: true
owl:inverse-of:: isPartOf
owl:domain:: Entity
owl:range:: Component

### requires
owl:iri:: https://metaverse-ontology.org/requires
owl:type:: ObjectProperty
owl:transitive:: true
owl:domain:: System
owl:range:: Requirement

### enables
owl:iri:: https://metaverse-ontology.org/enables
owl:type:: ObjectProperty
owl:domain:: Technology
owl:range:: Capability

## Data Properties

### term-id
owl:iri:: https://metaverse-ontology.org/termId
owl:type:: DataProperty
owl:functional:: true
owl:domain:: Concept
owl:range:: xsd:integer

### definition
owl:iri:: https://metaverse-ontology.org/definition
owl:type:: DataProperty
owl:domain:: Concept
owl:range:: xsd:string

### maturity
owl:iri:: https://metaverse-ontology.org/maturity
owl:type:: DataProperty
owl:domain:: Concept
owl:range:: MaturityLevel  # Enumeration

## Annotation Properties

### source
owl:iri:: https://metaverse-ontology.org/source
owl:type:: AnnotationProperty
owl:range:: xsd:string

### synonyms
owl:iri:: https://metaverse-ontology.org/synonyms
owl:type:: AnnotationProperty
owl:range:: xsd:string
```

## Export Script Requirements

You'll need a Rust/Python script to convert markdown → OWL:

### Basic Conversion Pipeline

```rust
// Pseudocode for conversion
use horned_owl::model::*;
use horned_owl::ontology::set::SetOntology;
use horned_functional;

fn markdown_to_owl(markdown_files: Vec<File>) -> SetOntology<String> {
    let mut ontology = SetOntology::new();
    
    // 1. Parse markdown files
    for file in markdown_files {
        let parsed = parse_markdown(file);
        
        // 2. Extract OWL structures
        if let Some(iri) = parsed.get_property("owl:iri") {
            // Create declaration
            let class = Class(IRI(iri.clone()));
            ontology.insert(Declaration::Class(class));
            
            // 3. Process axioms
            if let Some(axioms) = parsed.get_property("owl:subclass-axioms") {
                for axiom_str in axioms {
                    let axiom = parse_functional_syntax(axiom_str);
                    ontology.insert(axiom);
                }
            }
            
            // 4. Process property assertions
            // ... convert Logseq properties to OWL property assertions
        }
    }
    
    ontology
}

fn validate_ontology(ontology: &SetOntology<String>) -> ValidationResult {
    // Use horned-owl's built-in validation
    // Check consistency, coherence, profile compliance
    horned_owl::validate(ontology)
}
```

### Python Alternative (using py-horned-owl)

```python
import pyhornedowl
from pathlib import Path

def convert_markdown_to_owl(markdown_dir: Path, output_file: Path):
    """Convert markdown ontology to OWL functional syntax."""
    
    # Create new ontology
    onto = pyhornedowl.PyIndexedOntology()
    
    # Process each markdown file
    for md_file in markdown_dir.glob("**/*.md"):
        parsed = parse_markdown_properties(md_file)
        
        # Add declarations
        if 'owl:iri' in parsed and 'owl:entity-type' in parsed:
            iri = parsed['owl:iri']
            entity_type = parsed['owl:entity-type']
            
            if entity_type == 'Class':
                onto.add_axiom(f"Declaration(Class({iri}))")
        
        # Add axioms from owl:functional-syntax block
        if 'owl:functional-syntax' in parsed:
            for axiom in parsed['owl:functional-syntax']:
                onto.add_axiom(axiom)
    
    # Validate
    is_consistent = onto.check_consistency()
    
    # Export
    onto.save_to_file(str(output_file), format='functional')
    
    return is_consistent
```

## Minimal vs. Full Approach

### Minimal (Start Here)

**Just add to existing pages:**

1. **IRI declarations**:
   ```markdown
   owl:iri:: https://metaverse-ontology.org/TermName
   owl:type:: Class
   ```

2. **One functional syntax block per page**:
   ```markdown
   owl:functional-syntax:: |
     Declaration(Class(mv:TermName))
     SubClassOf(mv:TermName mv:ParentClass)
   ```

3. **Create PropertySchema.md** with property type declarations

### Full (Production Ready)

Add all structures mentioned above:
- Complete entity declarations
- Full axiom blocks
- Property characteristics
- Validation rules
- Export formats
- Consistency checks

## Validation Workflow

### Step 1: Prepare Markdown

Add OWL structures to your existing Logseq pages (see templates above).

### Step 2: Export to OWL

Run conversion script:

```bash
# Using custom Rust tool
cargo run --release -- convert \
  --input ./logseq_pages/ \
  --output metaverse_ontology.ofn \
  --format functional

# Using Python
python markdown_to_owl.py \
  --input ./logseq_pages/ \
  --output metaverse_ontology.ofn
```

### Step 3: Validate with Horned-Owl

```bash
# Using horned-bin CLI tools
horned validate metaverse_ontology.ofn

# Check for:
# - Consistency (no contradictions)
# - Coherence (all classes satisfiable)
# - Profile compliance (OWL 2 DL, EL, QL, etc.)
```

### Step 4: Fix Issues

Based on validation errors:

```markdown
# Common Issues & Fixes

## Issue: Undeclared entity
Error: Class mv:Avatar used but not declared
Fix: Add owl:iri:: and owl:type:: Class

## Issue: Domain/range violation  
Error: Property mv:hasUser has wrong range
Fix: Declare property domain and range explicitly

## Issue: Unsatisfiable class
Error: Class mv:VirtualPhysicalObject is unsatisfiable
Fix: Check for contradictory axioms (disjoint classes)
```

## Benefits of OWL-Compatible Structure

✅ **Formal validation** - Catch logical errors  
✅ **Reasoning** - Infer implicit relationships  
✅ **Interoperability** - Export to standard formats  
✅ **Tool support** - Use Protégé, Jena, etc.  
✅ **Standards compliance** - Follow W3C OWL 2 spec  
✅ **Performance** - horned-owl handles millions of terms  

## Integration with Existing Logseq Workflow

Your current workflow remains unchanged - the OWL structures are **additive**:

```markdown
# [[Avatar]] - Your Existing Page

## Core Properties ← KEEP AS-IS
term-id:: 20067
preferred-term:: Avatar
definition:: Digital representation...

## Ontological Relationships ← KEEP AS-IS  
is-a:: [[Digital Representation]]
has-part:: [[Visual Model]]

## OWL Export ← ADD THIS SECTION
owl:iri:: https://metaverse-ontology.org/Avatar
owl:type:: Class
owl:functional-syntax:: |
  Declaration(Class(mv:Avatar))
  SubClassOf(mv:Avatar mv:DigitalRepresentation)
  SubClassOf(mv:Avatar ObjectSomeValuesFrom(mv:hasPart mv:VisualModel))
```

## Recommended Tools

1. **horned-bin** - CLI for OWL operations
2. **py-horned-owl** - Python bindings
3. **Protégé** - Visual ontology editor (for verification)
4. **ROBOT** - Ontology transformation tool
5. **Custom converter** - Markdown → OWL pipeline

## Next Steps

1. **Phase 1**: Add minimal OWL structures (IRIs + functional syntax blocks)
2. **Phase 2**: Create PropertySchema.md and OntologyMetadata.md
3. **Phase 3**: Build markdown→OWL conversion script
4. **Phase 4**: Integrate horned-owl validation into CI/CD
5. **Phase 5**: Iterate based on validation feedback

## Summary

To use horned-owl for validation, add these **key engineering structures** to your markdown:

1. **IRI declarations** for all entities
2. **Entity type declarations** (Class, ObjectProperty, DataProperty)
3. **Formal axioms** in OWL Functional Syntax
4. **Property schemas** with domains, ranges, characteristics  
5. **Ontology metadata** with imports and prefixes
6. **Validation configuration** for profile and checks

The beauty of this approach: your markdown remains **human-readable** while being **machine-validatable**! 🎯

## Example 1: Avatar (Fully Completed)

```markdown
# Avatar

## Core Properties
term-id:: 20067
preferred-term:: Avatar
definition:: Digital representation of a person or agent used to interact within a virtual environment
maturity:: mature
source:: [[ACM + Web3D HAnim]]

## Classification
domain:: [[ETSI Domain/Interaction]]
layer:: [[User Experience Layer]]
aspect:: [[Visualization]], [[Social Interaction]]

## Ontological Relationships

### Taxonomic
is-a:: [[Digital Representation]]
subclass-of:: [[Virtual Entity]]
instance-of:: [[User Interface Element]]

### Compositional
has-part::
  - [[Visual Mesh]]
  - [[Animation Rig]]
  - [[Texture Maps]]
  - [[Collision Geometry]]
  - [[Audio Source]]

consists-of::
  - [[Body Model]]
  - [[Facial Expressions]]
  - [[Gesture System]]

### Dependency
requires::
  - [[3D Rendering Engine]]
  - [[Motion Capture System]] (optional)
  - [[User Input Controller]]
  - [[Network Synchronization]]

depends-on::
  - [[Avatar Standard]] (ISO/IEC 19774)
  - [[Graphics Pipeline]]

### Capability
enables::
  - [[User Embodiment]]
  - [[Social Presence]]
  - [[Non-verbal Communication]]
  - [[Identity Expression]]
  - [[Spatial Interaction]]

supports::
  - [[Multiplayer Interaction]]
  - [[Virtual Commerce]]
  - [[Social VR]]

### Association
related-to::
  - [[Virtual World]]
  - [[User Identity]]
  - [[Digital Twin]]
  - [[Metaverse]]
  
used-in::
  - [[Virtual Reality Applications]]
  - [[Online Games]]
  - [[Virtual Conferences]]
  - [[Social Platforms]]

implements:: [[H-Anim Specification]]

## Terminology
synonyms:: [[Virtual Persona]], [[Digital Identity]], [[User Representation]]
variant-terms:: [[Virtual Character]], [[Digital Avatar]]
see-also:: [[Proxy]], [[Agent]], [[Virtual Human]]

## Technical Details
standard-format:: glTF 2.0, FBX, USD
animation-standard:: [[H-Anim]]
interoperability-profile:: [[Avatar Interoperability]]

## Sources & References
primary-source:: [[ACM Metaverse Glossary]]
additional-sources:: Web3D HAnim WG · ISO/IEC 19774-2 · MSF Interoperable Avatars WG
standards-reference:: [[ISO/IEC 19774-1]], [[Web3D H-Anim]]

## Use Cases
- Virtual meetings and collaboration
- Gaming and entertainment
- Virtual retail and try-before-you-buy
- Training and education simulations
- Healthcare therapy applications

## Notes
Represents user embodiment or identification across virtual environments and platforms. Critical for social interaction and user presence in metaverse applications. Increasingly important for cross-platform identity and interoperability.

## Metadata
imported-from:: [[Metaverse Glossary Excel]]
import-date:: [[2025-01-15]]
ontology-status:: complete
last-reviewed:: [[2025-01-15]]
reviewed-by:: Ontology Team
```

```markdown
# Digital Twin

## Core Properties
term-id:: 20213

## Classification

layer:: [[Data Layer]], [[Application Layer]]

  - [[Supply Chain Optimization]]

  - Real-time insights
  - Historical analysis
  - Predictive analytics
  - Optimization recommendations

  - [[Physical Asset]]
  - [[IoT Platform]]
  - [[Simulation]]
  - [[Metaverse]]

  - [[PLM]] (Product Lifecycle Management)

  - [[Manufacturing]]
  - [[Healthcare]]
  - [[Smart Cities]]
  - [[Aerospace]]
  - [[Energy Sector]]
  - [[Automotive]]

implements::
  - [[ISO/IEC 23247 Framework]]
  - [[DTDL]] (Digital Twin Definition Language)

## Terminology
synonyms:: [[Virtual Replica]], [[Cyber Twin]], [[Digital Counterpart]]
variant-terms:: [[Device Shadow]], [[Virtual Prototype]], [[Digital Thread]]

not-to-be-confused-with:: [[3D Model]] (static, no synchronization)

data-flow:: Physical → Sensors → Edge → Cloud → Digital Twin → Analytics
update-frequency:: Real-time to near-real-time
synchronization-type:: Bidirectional
communication-protocol:: [[MQTT]], [[OPC UA]], [[DDS]]

  - [[Industrial Internet Consortium]]
  - [[ETSI]]
  - [[IEEE]]

  - ISO/IEC 23247-1 (Concepts)
  - ISO/IEC 23247-2 (Reference Architecture)

## Maturity & Adoption
adoption-stage:: Early mainstream
market-growth:: High
key-vendors:: Siemens, GE, Microsoft, AWS, PTC, Dassault Systèmes

## Notes
Digital Twins represent one of the key convergence points between physical and virtual worlds. They bridge IoT, AI, simulation, and visualization to create actionable intelligence from physical assets. Critical enabler for Industry 4.0 and smart infrastructure initiatives. Growing importance in metaverse applications for industrial and urban scenarios.

## Research Directions
```
